title="Collapse sidebar" aria-label="Collapse sidebar" class="button button--secondary button--outline collapseSidebarButton_PEFL"><svg width="20" height="20" aria-hidden="true" class="collapseSidebarButtonIcon_kv0_"><g fill="#7a7a7a"><path d="M9.992 10.023c0 .2-.062.399-.172.547l-4.996 7.492a.982.982 0 01-.828.454H1c-.55 0-1-.453-1-1 0-.2.059-.403.168-.551l4.629-6.942L.168 3.078A.939.939 0 010 2.528c0-.548.45-.997 1-.997h2.996c.352 0 .649.18.828.45L9.82 9.472c.11.148.172.347.172.55zm0 0"></path><path d="M19.98 10.023c0 .2-.058.399-.168.547l-4.996 7.492a.987.987 0 0"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></aside><main class="docMainContainer_TBSr"><div class="container padding-top--md padding-bottom--lg"><div class="row"><div class="col docItemCol_z5aJ"><div class="docItemContainer_c0TR"><article><nav class="theme-doc-breadcrumbs breadcrumbsContainer_Z_bl" aria-label="Breadcrumbs"><ul class="breadcrumbs"><li class="breadcrumbs__item"><a class="breadcrumbs__link" href="/weaviate/api"><span>APIs</span></a></li><li class="breadcrumbs__item"><a class="breadcrumbs__link" href="/weaviate/api/graphql"><span>Search API - GraphQL/gRPC</span></a></li><li class="breadcrumbs__item breadcrumbs__item--active"><span class="breadcrumbs__link">Search operators</span></li></ul></nav><div class="tocCollapsible_ETCw theme-doc-toc-mobile tocMobile_ITEo"><button type="button" class="clean-btn tocCollapsibleButton_TO0P">On this page</button></div><div class="theme-doc-markdown markdown"><header><h1>Search operators</h1></header>
<p>This page covers the search operators that can be used in queries, such as vector search operators (<code>nearText</code>, <code>nearVector</code>, <code>nearObject</code>, etc), keyword search operator (<code>bm25</code>), hybrid search operator (<code>hybrid</code>).</p>
<p>Only one search operator can be added to queries on the collection level.</p>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="operator-availability">Operator availability<a href="#operator-availability" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Operator availability" title="Direct link to Operator availability" translate="no">â€‹</a></h2>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="built-in-operators">Built-in operators<a href="#built-in-operators" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Built-in operators" title="Direct link to Built-in operators" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<p>These operators are available in all Weaviate instances regardless of configuration.</p>
<ul>
<li class=""><a href="#nearvector" class="">nearVector</a></li>
<li class=""><a href="#nearobject" class="">nearObject</a></li>
<li class=""><a href="#hybrid" class="">hybrid</a></li>
<li class=""><a href="#bm25" class="">bm25</a></li>
</ul>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="module-specific-operators">Module-specific operators<a href="#module-specific-operators" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Module-specific operators" title="Direct link to Module-specific operators" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<p>Module-specific search operators are made available in certain Weaviate modules.</p>
<p>By adding relevant modules, you can use the following operators:</p>
<ul>
<li class=""><a href="#neartext" class="">nearText</a></li>
<li class=""><a href="#multimodal-search" class="">Multimodal search</a></li>
<li class=""><a href="#ask" class="">ask</a></li>
</ul>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="vector-search-operators">Vector search operators<a href="#vector-search-operators" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Vector search operators" title="Direct link to Vector search operators" translate="no">â€‹</a></h2>
<p><code>nearXXX</code> operators allow you to find data objects based on their vector similarity to the query. They query can be a raw vector (<code>nearVector</code>) or an object UUID (<code>nearObject</code>).</p>
<p>If the appropriate vectorizer model is enabled, a text query (<code>nearText</code>), an image (<code>nearImage</code>), or another media input may be be used as the query.</p>
<p>All vector search operators can be used with a <code>certainty</code> or <code>distance</code> threshold specified, as well as a <a class="" href="/weaviate/api/graphql/additional-operators#limit-argument"><code>limit</code> operator</a> or an <a class="" href="/weaviate/api/graphql/additional-operators#autocut"><code>autocut</code> operator</a> to specify the desired similarity or distance between the query and the results</p>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="nearvector">nearVector<a href="#nearvector" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to nearVector" title="Direct link to nearVector" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<p><code>nearVector</code> finds data objects closest to an input vector.</p>
<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="variables">Variables<a href="#variables" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Variables" title="Direct link to Variables" translate="no">â€‹</a></h4>
<table><thead><tr><th>Variable</th><th>Required</th><th>Type</th><th>Description</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><code>vector</code></td><td>yes</td><td><code>[float]</code></td><td>This variable takes a vector embedding in the form of an array of floats. The array should have the same length as the vectors in this collection.</td></tr><tr><td><code>distance</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>float</code></td><td>The maximum allowed distance to the provided search input. Cannot be used together with the <code>certainty</code> variable. The interpretation of the value of the distance field depends on the <a class="" href="/weaviate/config-refs/distances">distance metric used</a>.</td></tr><tr><td><code>certainty</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>float</code></td><td>Normalized Distance between the result item and the search vector. Normalized to be between 0 (perfect opposite) and 1 (identical vectors). Can&#x27;t be used together with the <code>distance</code> variable.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="example">Example<a href="#example" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Example" title="Direct link to Example" translate="no">â€‹</a></h4>

<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="nearobject">nearObject<a href="#nearobject" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to nearObject" title="Direct link to nearObject" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<p><code>nearVector</code> finds data objects closest to an existing object in the same collection. The object is typically specified by its UUID.</p>
<ul>
<li class="">Note: You can specify an object&#x27;s <code>id</code> or <code>beacon</code> in the argument, along with a desired <code>certainty</code>.</li>
<li class="">Note that the first result will always be the object used for search.</li>
</ul>
<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="variables-1">Variables<a href="#variables-1" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Variables" title="Direct link to Variables" translate="no">â€‹</a></h4>
<table><thead><tr><th>Variable</th><th>Required</th><th>Type</th><th>Description</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><code>id</code></td><td>yes</td><td><code>UUID</code></td><td>Data object identifier in the uuid format.</td></tr><tr><td><code>beacon</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>url</code></td><td>Data object identifier in the beacon URL format. E.g., <code>weaviate://&lt;hostname&gt;/&lt;kind&gt;/id</code>.</td></tr><tr><td><code>distance</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>float</code></td><td>The maximum allowed distance to the provided search input. Cannot be used together with the <code>certainty</code> variable. The interpretation of the value of the distance field depends on the <a class="" href="/weaviate/config-refs/distances">distance metric used</a>.</td></tr><tr><td><code>certainty</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>float</code></td><td>Normalized Distance between the result item and the search vector. Normalized to be between 0 (perfect opposite) and 1 (identical vectors). Can&#x27;t be used together with the <code>distance</code> variable.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="example-1">Example<a href="#example-1" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Example" title="Direct link to Example" translate="no">â€‹</a></h4>

<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="neartext">nearText<a href="#neartext" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to nearText" title="Direct link to nearText" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<p>The <code>nearText</code> operator finds data objects based on their vector similarity to a natural language query.</p>
<p>This operator is enabled if a compatible vectorizer module is configured for the collection. Compatible vectorizer modules are:</p>
<ul>
<li class="">Any <code>text2vec</code> module</li>
<li class="">Any <code>multi2vec</code> module</li>
</ul>
<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="variables-2">Variables<a href="#variables-2" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Variables" title="Direct link to Variables" translate="no">â€‹</a></h4>
<table><thead><tr><th>Variable</th><th>Required</th><th>Type</th><th>Description</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><code>concepts</code></td><td>yes</td><td><code>[string]</code></td><td>An array of strings that can be natural language queries, or single words. If multiple strings are used, a centroid is calculated and used. Learn more about how the concepts are parsed <a href="#concept-parsing" class="">here</a>.</td></tr><tr><td><code>distance</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>float</code></td><td>The maximum allowed distance to the provided search input. Cannot be used together with the <code>certainty</code> variable. The interpretation of the value of the distance field depends on the <a class="" href="/weaviate/config-refs/distances">distance metric used</a>.</td></tr><tr><td><code>certainty</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>float</code></td><td>Normalized Distance between the result item and the search vector. Normalized to be between 0 (perfect opposite) and 1 (identical vectors). Can&#x27;t be used together with the <code>distance</code> variable.</td></tr><tr><td><code>autocorrect</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>boolean</code></td><td>Autocorrect input text values. Requires the <a class="" href="/weaviate/modules/spellcheck"><code>text-spellcheck</code> module</a> to be present &amp; enabled.</td></tr><tr><td><code>moveTo</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>object{}</code></td><td>Move your search term closer to another vector described by keywords</td></tr><tr><td><code>moveTo{concepts}</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>[string]</code></td><td>An array of strings - natural language queries or single words. If multiple strings are used, a centroid is calculated and used.</td></tr><tr><td><code>moveTo{objects}</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>[UUID]</code></td><td>Object IDs to move the results to. This is used to &quot;bias&quot; NLP search results into a certain direction in vector space.</td></tr><tr><td><code>moveTo{force}</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>float</code></td><td>The force to apply to a particular movement. Must be between 0 and 1 where 0 is equivalent to no movement and 1 is equivalent to largest movement possible.</td></tr><tr><td><code>moveAwayFrom</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>object{}</code></td><td>Move your search term away from another vector described by keywords</td></tr><tr><td><code>moveAwayFrom{concepts}</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>[string]</code></td><td>An array of strings - natural language queries or single words. If multiple strings are used, a centroid is calculated and used.</td></tr><tr><td><code>moveAwayFrom{objects}</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>[UUID]</code></td><td>Object IDs to move the results from. This is used to &quot;bias&quot; NLP search results into a certain direction in vector space.</td></tr><tr><td><code>moveAwayFrom{force}</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>float</code></td><td>The force to apply to a particular movement. Must be between 0 and 1 where 0 is equivalent to no movement and 1 is equivalent to largest movement possible.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="example-i">Example I<a href="#example-i" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Example I" title="Direct link to Example I" translate="no">â€‹</a></h4>
<p>This example shows an example usage the <code>nearText</code> operator, including how to bias results towards another search query.</p>

<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="example-ii">Example II<a href="#example-ii" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Example II" title="Direct link to Example II" translate="no">â€‹</a></h4>
<p>You can also bias results toward other data objects. For example, in this query, we move our query about &quot;travelling in asia&quot;, towards an article on food.</p>

<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="additional-information">Additional information<a href="#additional-information" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Additional information" title="Direct link to Additional information" translate="no">â€‹</a></h4>
<h5 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="concept-parsing">Concept parsing<a href="#concept-parsing" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Concept parsing" title="Direct link to Concept parsing" translate="no">â€‹</a></h5>
<p>A <code>nearText</code> query will interpret each term in an array input as distinct strings to be vectorized. If multiple strings are passed, the query vector will be an average vector of the individual string vectors.</p>
<ul>
<li class=""><code>[&quot;New York Times&quot;]</code> = one vector position is determined based on the occurrences of the words</li>
<li class=""><code>[&quot;New&quot;, &quot;York&quot;, &quot;Times&quot;]</code> = all concepts have a similar weight.</li>
<li class=""><code>[&quot;New York&quot;, &quot;Times&quot;]</code> = a combination of the two above.</li>
</ul>
<p>A practical example would be: <code>concepts: [&quot;beatles&quot;, &quot;John Lennon&quot;]</code></p>
<h5 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="semantic-path">Semantic Path<a href="#semantic-path" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Semantic Path" title="Direct link to Semantic Path" translate="no">â€‹</a></h5>
<ul>
<li class="">Only available in <code>txt2vec-contextionary</code> module</li>
</ul>
<p>The semantic path returns an array of concepts from the query to the data object. This allows you to see which steps Weaviate took and how the query and data object are interpreted.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Property</th><th>Description</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><code>concept</code></td><td>the concept that is found in this step.</td></tr><tr><td><code>distanceToNext</code></td><td>the distance to the next step (null for the last step).</td></tr><tr><td><code>distanceToPrevious</code></td><td>this distance to the previous step (null for the first step).</td></tr><tr><td><code>distanceToQuery</code></td><td>the distance of this step to the query.</td></tr><tr><td><code>distanceToResult</code></td><td>the distance of the step to this result.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><em>Note: Building a semantic path is only possible if a <a href="#neartext" class=""><code>nearText: {}</code> operator</a> is set as the explore term represents the beginning of the path and each search result represents the end of the path. Since <code>nearText: {}</code> queries are currently exclusively possible in GraphQL, the <code>semanticPath</code> is therefore not available in the REST API.</em></p>
<p>Example: showing a semantic path without edges.</p>

style="color:#393A34">}</span><span class="token plain"></span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain"></span><span class="token punctuation" <h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="multimodal-search">Multimodal search<a href="#multimodal-search" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Multimodal search" title="Direct link to Multimodal search" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<p>Depending on the vectorizer module, you can use additional modalities such as images, audio, or video as the query, and retrieve corresponding, compatible objects.</p>
<p>Some modules, such as <code>multi2vec-clip</code> and <code>multi2vec-bind</code> allow you to search across modalities. For example, you can search for images using a text query, or search for text using an image query.</p>
<p>For more information, see specific module pages such as these:</p>
<ul>
<li class=""><a class="" href="/weaviate/model-providers/transformers/embeddings-multimodal">Transformers multimodal embeddings</a></li>
<li class=""><a class="" href="/weaviate/model-providers/imagebind/embeddings-multimodal">ImageBind multimodal embeddings</a></li>
</ul>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="hybrid">hybrid<a href="#hybrid" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to hybrid" title="Direct link to hybrid" translate="no">â€‹</a></h2>
<p>This operator allows you to combine <a href="#bm25" class="">BM25</a> and vector search to get a &quot;best of both worlds&quot; type search results set.</p>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="variables-3">Variables<a href="#variables-3" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Variables" title="Direct link to Variables" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<table><thead><tr><th>Variables</th><th>Required</th><th>Type</th><th>Description</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><code>query</code></td><td>yes</td><td><code>string</code></td><td>search query</td></tr><tr><td><code>alpha</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>float</code></td><td>weighting for each search algorithm, default 0.75</td></tr><tr><td><code>vector</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>[float]</code></td><td>optional to supply your own vector</td></tr><tr><td><code>properties</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>[string]</code></td><td>list of properties to limit the BM25 search to, default all text properties</td></tr><tr><td><code>fusionType</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>string</code></td><td>the type of hybrid fusion algorithm (available from <code>v1.20.0</code>)</td></tr><tr><td><code>bm25SearchOperator</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>object</code></td><td>set how many of the (bm25) query tokens must be present in the target object for it to be considered a match. (available from <code>v1.31.0</code>)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<ul>
<li class="">Notes:<!-- -->
<ul>
<li class=""><code>alpha</code> can be any number from 0 to 1, defaulting to 0.75.<!-- -->
<ul>
<li class=""><code>alpha</code> = 0 forces using a pure <strong>keyword</strong> search method (BM25)</li>
<li class=""><code>alpha</code> = 1 forces using a pure <strong>vector</strong> search method</li>
<li class=""><code>alpha</code> = 0.5 weighs the BM25 and vector methods evenly</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li class=""><code>fusionType</code> can be <code>rankedFusion</code> or <code>relativeScoreFusion</code>
<ul>
<li class=""><code>rankedFusion</code> (default) adds inverted ranks of the BM25 and vector search methods</li>
<li class=""><code>relativeScoreFusion</code> adds normalized scores of the BM25 and vector search methods</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="fusion-algorithms">Fusion algorithms<a href="#fusion-algorithms" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Fusion algorithms" title="Direct link to Fusion algorithms" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="ranked-fusion">Ranked fusion<a href="#ranked-fusion" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Ranked fusion" title="Direct link to Ranked fusion" translate="no">â€‹</a></h4>
<p>The <code>rankedFusion</code> algorithm is Weaviate&#x27;s original hybrid fusion algorithm.</p>
<p>In this algorithm, each object is scored according to its position in the results for that search (vector or keyword). The top-ranked objects in each search get the highest scores. Scores decrease going from top to least ranked. The total score is calculated by adding the rank-based scores from the vector and keyword searches.</p>
<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="relative-score-fusion">Relative score fusion<a href="#relative-score-fusion" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Relative score fusion" title="Direct link to Relative score fusion" translate="no">â€‹</a></h4>
<div class="theme-admonition theme-admonition-info admonition_xJq3 alert alert--info"><div class="admonitionHeading_Gvgb"><span class="admonitionIcon_Rf37"><svg viewBox="0 0 14 16"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7 2.3c3.14 0 5.7 2.56 5.7 5.7s-2.56 5.7-5.7 5.7A5.71 5.71 0 0 1 1.3 8c0-3.14 2.56-5.7 5.7-5.7zM7 1C3.14 1 0 4.14 0 8s3.14 7 7 7 7-3.14 7-7-3.14-7-7-7zm1 3H6v5h2V4zm0 6H6v2h2v-2z"></path></svg></span>Added in <code>v1.20</code></div></div>
<div class="theme-admonition theme-admonition-info admonition_xJq3 alert alert--info"><div class="admonitionHeading_Gvgb"><span class="admonitionIcon_Rf37"><svg viewBox="0 0 14 16"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7 2.3c3.14 0 5.7 2.56 5.7 5.7s-2.56 5.7-5.7 5.7A5.71 5.71 0 0 1 1.3 8c0-3.14 2.56-5.7 5.7-5.7zM7 1C3.14 1 0 4.14 0 8s3.14 7 7 7 7-3.14 7-7-3.14-7-7-7zm1 3H6v5h2V4zm0 6H6v2h2v-2z"></path></svg></span>Relative Score Fusion is the default in <code>v1.24</code> and higher.</div></div>
<p>In <code>relativeScoreFusion</code> the vector search and keyword search scores are scaled between <code>0</code> and <code>1</code>. The highest raw score becomes <code>1</code> in the scaled scores. The lowest value is assigned <code>0</code>. The remaining values are ranked between <code>0</code> and <code>1</code>. The total score is a scaled sum of the normalized vector similarity and normalized BM25 scores.</p>
<details class="details_lb9f alert alert--info details_b_Ee" data-collapsed="true"><summary>Fusion scoring comparison</summary><div><div class="collapsibleContent_i85q"><p>This example uses a small search result set to compare the ranked fusion and relative fusion algorithms. The table shows the following information:</p><ul>
<li class=""><code>document id</code>, from 0 to 4</li>
<li class=""><code>keyword score</code>, sorted</li>
<li class=""><code>vector search score</code>, sorted</li>
</ul><table><tr><th>Search Type</th><th>(id): score</th><th>(id): score</th><th>(id): score</th><th>(id): score</th><th>(id): score</th></tr><tr><td>Keyword</td><td>(1): 5</td><td>(0): 2.6</td><td>(2): 2.3</td><td>(4): 0.2</td><td>(3): 0.09</td></tr><tr><td>Vector</td><td>(2): 0.6</td><td>(4): 0.598</td><td>(0): 0.596</td><td>(1): 0.594</td><td>(3): 0.009</td></tr></table><p>The ranking algorithms use these scores to derive the hybrid ranking.</p><h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="ranked-fusion-1">Ranked fusion<a href="#ranked-fusion-1" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Ranked fusion" title="Direct link to Ranked fusion" translate="no">â€‹</a></h4><p>The score depends on the rank of the result. The score is equal to <code>1/(RANK + 60)</code>:</p><table><tr><th>Search Type</th><th>(id): score</th><th>(id): score</th><th>(id): score</th><th>(id): score</th><th>(id): score</th></tr><tr><td>Keyword</td><td>(1): 0.0154</td><td>(0): 0.0160</td><td>(2): 0.0161</td><td>(4): 0.0167</td><td>(3): 0.0166</td></tr><tr><td>Vector</td><td>(2): 0.016502</td><td>(4): 0.016502</td><td>(0): 0.016503</td><td>(1): 0.016503</td><td>(3): 0.016666</td></tr></table><p>As you can see, the results of each rank is identical, regardless of the input score.</p><h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="relative-score-fusion-1">Relative score fusion<a href="#relative-score-fusion-1" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Relative score fusion" title="Direct link to Relative score fusion" translate="no">â€‹</a></h4><p>Here, we normalize the scores â€“ the largest score is set to 1 and the lowest to 0, and all entries in-between are scaled according to their <strong>relative distance</strong> to the <strong>maximum</strong> and <strong>minimum values</strong>.</p><table><tr><th>Search Type</th><th>(id): score</th><th>(id): score</th><th>(id): score</th><th>(id): score</th><th>(id): score</th></tr><tr><td>Keyword</td><td>(1): 1.0</td><td>(0): 0.511</td><td>(2): 0.450</td><td>(4): 0.022</td><td>(3): 0.0</td></tr><tr><td>Vector</td><td>(2): 1.0</td><td>(4): 0.996</td><td>(0): 0.993</td><td>(1): 0.986</td><td>(3): 0.0</td></tr></table><p>Here, the scores reflect the relative distribution of the original scores. For example, the vector search scores of the first 4 documents were almost identical, which is still the case for the normalized scores.</p><h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="weighting--final-scores">Weighting &amp; final scores<a href="#weighting--final-scores" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Weighting &amp; final scores" title="Direct link to Weighting &amp; final scores" translate="no">â€‹</a></h4><p>Before adding these scores up, they are weighted according to the alpha parameter. Letâ€™s assume <code>alpha=0.5</code>, meaning both search types contribute equally to the final result and therefore each score is multiplied by 0.5.</p><p>Now, we can add the scores for each document up and compare the results from both fusion algorithms.</p><table><tr><th>Algorithm Type</th><th>(id): score</th><th>(id): score</th><th>(id): score</th><th>(id): score</th><th>(id): score</th></tr><tr><td>Ranked</td><td>(2): 0.016301</td><td>(1): 0.015952</td><td>(0): 0.015952</td><td>(4): 0.016600</td><td>(3): 0.016630</td></tr><tr><td>Relative</td><td>(1): 0.993</td><td>(0): 0.752</td><td>(2): 0.725</td><td>(4): 0.509</td><td>(3): 0.0</td></tr></table><h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="what-can-we-learn-from-this">What can we learn from this?<a href="#what-can-we-learn-from-this" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to What can we learn from this?" title="Direct link to What can we learn from this?" translate="no">â€‹</a></h4><p>For the vector search, the scores for the top 4 objects (<strong>IDs 2, 4, 0, 1</strong>) were almost identical, and all of them were good results. While for the keyword search, one object (<strong>ID 1</strong>) was much better than the rest.</p><p>This is captured in the final result of <code>relativeScoreFusion</code>, which identified the object <strong>ID 1</strong> the top result. This is justified because this document was the best result in the keyword search with a big gap to the next-best score and in the top group of vector search.</p><p>In contrast, for <code>rankedFusion</code>, the object <strong>ID 2</strong> is the top result, closely followed by objects <strong>ID 1</strong> and <strong>ID 0</strong>.</p></div></div></details>
<p>For a fuller discussion of fusion methods, see <a href="https://weaviate.io/blog/hybrid-search-fusion-algorithms" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">this blog post</a></p>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="additional-metadata-response">Additional metadata response<a href="#additional-metadata-response" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Additional metadata response" title="Direct link to Additional metadata response" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<p>Hybrid search results are sorted by a score, derived as a fused combination of their BM25F score and <code>nearText</code> similarity (higher is more relevant). This <code>score</code>, and additionally the <code>explainScore</code> metadata can be optionally retrieved in the response.</p>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="example-2">Example<a href="#example-2" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Example" title="Direct link to Example" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>

<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="example-with-vector-specified">Example with vector specified<a href="#example-with-vector-specified" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Example with vector specified" title="Direct link to Example with vector specified" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<p>You can optionally supply the vector query to the <code>vector</code> variable. This will override the <code>query</code> variable for the vector search component of the hybrid search.</p>

<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="hybrid-with-a-conditional-filter">Hybrid with a conditional filter<a href="#hybrid-with-a-conditional-filter" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Hybrid with a conditional filter" title="Direct link to Hybrid with a conditional filter" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<div class="theme-admonition theme-admonition-info admonition_xJq3 alert alert--info"><div class="admonitionHeading_Gvgb"><span class="admonitionIcon_Rf37"><svg viewBox="0 0 14 16"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7 2.3c3.14 0 5.7 2.56 5.7 5.7s-2.56 5.7-5.7 5.7A5.71 5.71 0 0 1 1.3 8c0-3.14 2.56-5.7 5.7-5.7zM7 1C3.14 1 0 4.14 0 8s3.14 7 7 7 7-3.14 7-7-3.14-7-7-7zm1 3H6v5h2V4zm0 6H6v2h2v-2z"></path></svg></span>Added in <code>v1.18.0</code></div></div>
<p>A <a class="" href="/weaviate/api/graphql/filters">conditional (<code>where</code>) filter</a> can be used with <code>hybrid</code>.</p>

<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="specify-object-properties-for-bm25-search">Specify object properties for BM25 search<a href="#specify-object-properties-for-bm25-search" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Specify object properties for BM25 search" title="Direct link to Specify object properties for BM25 search" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<div class="theme-admonition theme-admonition-info admonition_xJq3 alert alert--info"><div class="admonitionHeading_Gvgb"><span class="admonitionIcon_Rf37"><svg viewBox="0 0 14 16"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7 2.3c3.14 0 5.7 2.56 5.7 5.7s-2.56 5.7-5.7 5.7A5.71 5.71 0 0 1 1.3 8c0-3.14 2.56-5.7 5.7-5.7zM7 1C3.14 1 0 4.14 0 8s3.14 7 7 7 7-3.14 7-7-3.14-7-7-7zm1 3H6v5h2V4zm0 6H6v2h2v-2z"></path></svg></span>Added in <code>v1.19</code></div></div>
<p>A <code>hybrid</code> operator can accept an array of strings to limit the set of properties for the BM25 component of the search. If unspecified, all text properties will be searched.</p>

<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="oversearch-with-relativescorefusion">Oversearch with <code>relativeScoreFusion</code><a href="#oversearch-with-relativescorefusion" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to oversearch-with-relativescorefusion" title="Direct link to oversearch-with-relativescorefusion" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<div class="theme-admonition theme-admonition-info admonition_xJq3 alert alert--info"><div class="admonitionHeading_Gvgb"><span class="admonitionIcon_Rf37"><svg viewBox="0 0 14 16"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7 2.3c3.14 0 5.7 2.56 5.7 5.7s-2.56 5.7-5.7 5.7A5.71 5.71 0 0 1 1.3 8c0-3.14 2.56-5.7 5.7-5.7zM7 1C3.14 1 0 4.14 0 8s3.14 7 7 7 7-3.14 7-7-3.14-7-7-7zm1 3H6v5h2V4zm0 6H6v2h2v-2z"></path></svg></span>Added in <code>v1.21</code></div></div>
<p>When <code>relativeScoreFusion</code> is used as the <code>fusionType</code> with a small search <code>limit</code>, a result set can be very sensitive to the limit parameter due to the normalization of the scores.</p>
<p>To mitigate this effect, Weaviate automatically performs a search with a higher limit (100) and then trims the results down to the requested limit.</p>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="bm25-search-operator">BM25 search operator<a href="#bm25-search-operator" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to BM25 search operator" title="Direct link to BM25 search operator" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<div class="theme-admonition theme-admonition-info admonition_xJq3 alert alert--info"><div class="admonitionHeading_Gvgb"><span class="admonitionIcon_Rf37"><svg viewBox="0 0 14 16"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7 2.3c3.14 0 5.7 2.56 5.7 5.7s-2.56 5.7-5.7 5.7A5.71 5.71 0 0 1 1.3 8c0-3.14 2.56-5.7 5.7-5.7zM7 1C3.14 1 0 4.14 0 8s3.14 7 7 7 7-3.14 7-7-3.14-7-7-7zm1 3H6v5h2V4zm0 6H6v2h2v-2z"></path></svg></span>Added in <code>v1.31</code></div></div>
<p>Use <code>bm25SearchOperator</code> to set how many of the query tokens must be present in the target object for it to be considered a match in the keyword (bm25) search portion of the hybrid search. This is useful when you want to ensure that only objects with a certain number of relevant keywords are returned.</p>
<p>The available options are <code>And</code>, or <code>Or</code>. If <code>Or</code> is set, an additional parameter <code>minimumOrTokensMatch</code> must be specified, which defines how many of the query tokens must match for the object to be considered a match.</p>
<p>If not yet, the keyword search will behave as if <code>Or</code> was set with <code>minimumOrTokensMatch</code> equal to 1.</p>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="bm25">BM25<a href="#bm25" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to BM25" title="Direct link to BM25" translate="no">â€‹</a></h2>
<p>The <code>bm25</code> operator performs a keyword (sparse vector) search, and uses the BM25F ranking function to score the results. BM25F (<strong>B</strong>est <strong>M</strong>atch <strong>25</strong> with Extension to Multiple Weighted <strong>F</strong>ields) is an extended version of BM25 that applies the scoring algorithm to multiple fields (<code>properties</code>), producing better results.</p>
<p>The search is case-insensitive, and case matching does not confer a score advantage. Stop words are removed. <a href="https://github.com/weaviate/weaviate/issues/2439" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">Stemming is not supported yet</a>.</p>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="schema-configuration">Schema configuration<a href="#schema-configuration" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Schema configuration" title="Direct link to Schema configuration" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<p>The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Okapi_BM25#The_ranking_function" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">free parameters <code>k1</code> and <code>b</code></a> are configurable and optional. See the <a class="" href="/weaviate/config-refs/indexing/inverted-index#bm25">schema reference</a> for more details.</p>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="variables-4">Variables<a href="#variables-4" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Variables" title="Direct link to Variables" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<p>The <code>bm25</code> operator supports the following variables:</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Variables</th><th>Required</th><th>Description</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><code>query</code></td><td>yes</td><td>The keyword search query.</td></tr><tr><td><code>properties</code></td><td>no</td><td>Array of properties (fields) to search in, defaulting to all properties in the collection.</td></tr><tr><td><code>searchOperator</code></td><td>no</td><td>set how many of the query tokens must be present in the target object for it to be considered a match. (available from <code>v1.31.0</code>)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="theme-admonition theme-admonition-info admonition_xJq3 alert alert--info"><div class="admonitionHeading_Gvgb"><span class="admonitionIcon_Rf37"><svg viewBox="0 0 14 16"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7 2.3c3.14 0 5.7 2.56 5.7 5.7s-2.56 5.7-5.7 5.7A5.71 5.71 0 0 1 1.3 8c0-3.14 2.56-5.7 5.7-5.7zM7 1C3.14 1 0 4.14 0 8s3.14 7 7 7 7-3.14 7-7-3.14-7-7-7zm1 3H6v5h2V4zm0 6H6v2h2v-2z"></path></svg></span>Boosting properties</div><div class="admonitionContent_BuS1"><p>Specific properties can be boosted by a factor specified as a number after the caret sign, for example <code>properties: [&quot;title^3&quot;, &quot;summary&quot;]</code>.</p></div></div>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="additional-metadata-response-1">Additional metadata response<a href="#additional-metadata-response-1" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Additional metadata response" title="Direct link to Additional metadata response" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<p>The BM25F <code>score</code> metadata can be optionally retrieved in the response. A higher score indicates higher relevance.</p>

<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="bm25-with-a-conditional-filter">BM25 with a conditional filter<a href="#bm25-with-a-conditional-filter" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to BM25 with a conditional filter" title="Direct link to BM25 with a conditional filter" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<div class="theme-admonition theme-admonition-info admonition_xJq3 alert alert--info"><div class="admonitionHeading_Gvgb"><span class="admonitionIcon_Rf37"><svg viewBox="0 0 14 16"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7 2.3c3.14 0 5.7 2.56 5.7 5.7s-2.56 5.7-5.7 5.7A5.71 5.71 0 0 1 1.3 8c0-3.14 2.56-5.7 5.7-5.7zM7 1C3.14 1 0 4.14 0 8s3.14 7 7 7 7-3.14 7-7-3.14-7-7-7zm1 3H6v5h2V4zm0 6H6v2h2v-2z"></path></svg></span>Added in <code>v1.18</code></div></div>
<p>A <a class="" href="/weaviate/api/graphql/filters">conditional (<code>where</code>) filter</a> can be used with <code>bm25</code>.</p>

<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="search-operator">Search operator<a href="#search-operator" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Search operator" title="Direct link to Search operator" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<div class="theme-admonition theme-admonition-info admonition_xJq3 alert alert--info"><div class="admonitionHeading_Gvgb"><span class="admonitionIcon_Rf37"><svg viewBox="0 0 14 16"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7 2.3c3.14 0 5.7 2.56 5.7 5.7s-2.56 5.7-5.7 5.7A5.71 5.71 0 0 1 1.3 8c0-3.14 2.56-5.7 5.7-5.7zM7 1C3.14 1 0 4.14 0 8s3.14 7 7 7 7-3.14 7-7-3.14-7-7-7zm1 3H6v5h2V4zm0 6H6v2h2v-2z"></path></svg></span>Added in <code>v1.31</code></div></div>
<p>Use <code>searchOperator</code> to set how many of the query tokens must be present in the target object for it to be considered a match. This is useful when you want to ensure that only objects with a certain number of relevant keywords are returned.</p>
<p>The available options are <code>And</code>, or <code>Or</code>. If <code>Or</code> is set, an additional parameter <code>minimumOrTokensMatch</code> must be specified, which defines how many of the query tokens must match for the object to be considered a match.</p>
<p>If not yet, the keyword search will behave as if <code>Or</code> was set with <code>minimumOrTokensMatch</code> equal to 1.</p>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="ask">ask<a href="#ask" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to ask" title="Direct link to ask" translate="no">â€‹</a></h2>
<p>Enabled by the module: <a class="" href="/weaviate/modules/qna-transformers">Question Answering</a>.</p>
<p>This operator allows you to return answers to questions by running the results through a Q&amp;A model.</p>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="variables-5">Variables<a href="#variables-5" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Variables" title="Direct link to Variables" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<table><thead><tr><th>Variable</th><th>Required</th><th>Type</th><th>Description</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><code>question</code></td><td>yes</td><td><code>string</code></td><td>The question to be answered.</td></tr><tr><td><code>certainty</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>float</code></td><td>Desired minimal certainty or confidence of answer to the question. The higher the value, the stricter the search becomes. The lower the value, the fuzzier the search becomes. If no certainty is set, any answer that could be extracted will be returned.</td></tr><tr><td><code>properties</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>[string]</code></td><td>The properties of the queries collection which contains text. If no properties are set, all are considered.</td></tr><tr><td><code>rerank</code></td><td>no</td><td><code>boolean</code></td><td>If enabled, the qna module will rerank the result based on the answer score. For example, if the 3rd result - as determined by the previous (semantic) search contained the most likely answer, result 3 will be pushed to position 1, etc. <em>Supported since v1.10.0</em></td></tr></tbody></table>

<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="additional-metadata-response-2">Additional metadata response<a href="#additional-metadata-response-2" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Additional metadata response" title="Direct link to Additional metadata response" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<p>The <code>answer</code> and a <code>certainty</code> can be retrieved.</p>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="questions-and-feedback">Questions and feedback<a href="#questions-and-feedback" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Questions and feedback" title="Direct link to Questions and feedback" translate="no">â€‹</a></h2>

<p>If you have any questions or feedback, let us know in the <a href="https://forum.weaviate.io/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" class="">user forum</a>.</p>
